            <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg/23px-Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg/35px-Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg/46px-Flag_of_Gibraltar.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
           </span>
           <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
            Gibraltar
           </a>
           <span style="font-weight:normal;">
            (
            <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
             United Kingdom
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </b>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>

      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Iberian Peninsula
       </b>
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">
            aɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪər/: 'ear' in 'near'">
            ɪər
           </span>
           <span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">
            i
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'p' in 'pie'">
            p
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/sj/: 's' in 'consume'">
            sj
           </span>
           <span title="/ʊ/: 'oo' in 'foot'">
            ʊ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [a]
        </a>
       </sup>
       also known as
       <b>
        Iberia
       </b>
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">
            aɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪər/: 'ear' in 'near'">
            ɪər
           </span>
           <span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">
            i
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [b]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is located in the southwest corner of
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">
        peninsula
       </a>
       is principally divided between
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       , comprising most of their territory. It also includes
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">
        Andorra
       </a>
       , and a small part of
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       along the peninsula's northeastern edge, as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar
       </a>
       on its south coast, a small peninsula that forms an
       <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">
        overseas territory of the United Kingdom
       </a>
       . With an area of approximately 582,000 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (225,000 sq mi), it is the second largest European peninsula, after the
       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Peninsula" title="Scandinavian Peninsula">
        Scandinavian
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">
        Name
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iberia_Europe_satfoto_2014067.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5200" data-file-width="6400" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Iberia_Europe_satfoto_2014067.jpg/300px-Iberia_Europe_satfoto_2014067.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Iberia_Europe_satfoto_2014067.jpg/450px-Iberia_Europe_satfoto_2014067.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Iberia_Europe_satfoto_2014067.jpg/600px-Iberia_Europe_satfoto_2014067.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iberia_Europe_satfoto_2014067.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Iberian Peninsula and southern France, satellite photo on a cloudless day in March 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_name">
        Greek name
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Greek name">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The word
       <i>
        Iberia
       </i>
       is a noun adapted from the Latin word "Hiberia" originated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">
        Ancient Greek
       </a>
       word Ἰβηρία (
       <i>
        Ibēría
       </i>
       ) by Greek geographers under the rule of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       to refer to what is known today in English as the Iberian Peninsula.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LyonsPapadopoulos2002_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LyonsPapadopoulos2002-3">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At that time, the name did not describe a single political entity or a distinct population of people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">
        Strabo
       </a>
       's 'Iberia' was delineated from Keltikē (
       <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">
        Gaul
       </a>
       ) by the Pyrenees
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ebel1976_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ebel1976-5">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and included the entire land mass southwest (he says "west") of there.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padrón2004_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Padrón2004-6">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The noun "Hiberia" fell into disuse when the Romans decided to call the most western part of the peninsula "Lusitania" (today Portugal) and the remaining territory as "Spania" (modern Spain). With the fall of the Roman Empire and the establishment of the new Castillian language in Spain, the word "Iberia" appeared for the first time in use as a direct 'descendant' of the Greek word "βηρία" and the Roman word "Hiberia".
      </p>
      <p>
       The ancient Greeks reached the Iberian Peninsula, of which they had heard from the Phoenicians, by voyaging westward on the Mediterranean.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaldmanMason2006_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WaldmanMason2006-7">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Hecataeus_of_Miletus" title="Hecataeus of Miletus">
        Hecataeus of Miletus
       </a>
       was the first known to use the term
       <i>
        Iberia
       </i>
       , which he wrote about circa 500 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">
        Herodotus
       </a>
       of Halicarnassus says of the
       <a href="/wiki/Phocaea" title="Phocaea">
        Phocaeans
       </a>
       that "it was they who made the Greeks acquainted with... Iberia."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herodotus1827_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Herodotus1827-9">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to
       <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">
        Strabo
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-III.4.19_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-III.4.19-10">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       prior historians used
       <i>
        Iberia
       </i>
       to mean the country "this side of the Ἶβηρος (
       <i>
        Ibēros
       </i>
       )" as far north as the river
       <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B4ne" title="Rhône">
        Rhône
       </a>
       in France, but currently they set the
       <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">
        Pyrenees
       </a>
       as the limit.
       <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">
        Polybius
       </a>
       respects that limit,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but identifies Iberia as the Mediterranean side as far south as
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar
       </a>
       , with the Atlantic side having no name. Elsewhere
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       he says that
       <a href="/wiki/Sagunto" title="Sagunto">
        Saguntum
       </a>
       is "on the seaward foot of the range of hills connecting Iberia and Celtiberia."
      </p>
      <p>
       Strabo
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       refers to the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carretanian&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carretanian (page does not exist)">
        Carretanians
       </a>
       as people "of the Iberian stock" living in the Pyrenees, who are distinct from either
       <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">
        Celts
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Celtiberians" title="Celtiberians">
        Celtiberians
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_names">
        Roman names
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Roman names">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_Ebel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Charles Ebel (page does not exist)">
        Charles Ebel
       </a>
       , the ancient sources in both Latin and Greek use Hispania and Hiberia (Greek: Iberia) as synonyms. The confusion of the words was because of an overlapping in political and geographic perspectives. The Latin word
       <i>
        Hiberia
       </i>
       , similar to the Greek
       <i>
        Iberia
       </i>
       , literally translates to "land of the Hiberians". This word was derived from the river Ebro, which the Romans called
       <i>
        Hiberus
       </i>
       .
       <i>
        Hiber
       </i>
       (Iberian) was thus used as a term for peoples living near the river Ebro.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ebel1976_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ebel1976-5">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaffiot1934_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gaffiot1934-14">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first mention in Roman literature was by the annalist poet
       <a href="/wiki/Ennius" title="Ennius">
        Ennius
       </a>
       in 200 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woolf2012_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Woolf2012-15">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vega2003_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Vega2003-17">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">
        Virgil
       </a>
       refers to the
       <i>
        Ipacatos Hiberos
       </i>
       ("restless Iberi") in his
       <a href="/wiki/Georgics" title="Georgics">
        Georgics
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Virgil1846_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Virgil1846-18">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Roman geographers and other prose writers from the time of the late
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Roman Republic
       </a>
       called the entire peninsula
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
         Hispania
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As they became politically interested in the former Carthaginian territories, the Romans began to use the names
       <i>
        Hispania Citerior
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Hispania Ulterior
       </i>
       for 'near' and 'far' Hispania. At the time Hispania was made up of three
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">
        Roman provinces
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Baetica" title="Hispania Baetica">
        Hispania Baetica
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Tarraconensis" title="Hispania Tarraconensis">
        Hispania Tarraconensis
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">
        Lusitania
       </a>
       . Strabo says
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-III.4.19_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-III.4.19-10">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       that the Romans use
       <i>
        Hispania
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Iberia
       </i>
       synonymously, distinguishing between the
       <i>
        near
       </i>
       northern and the
       <i>
        far
       </i>
       southern provinces. (The name "Iberia" was ambiguous, being also the name of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iberia" title="Kingdom of Iberia">
        Kingdom of Iberia
       </a>
       in the Caucasus.)
      </p>
      <p>
       Whatever language may generally have been spoken on the peninsula soon gave way to Latin, except for that of the
       <a href="/wiki/Vascones" title="Vascones">
        Vascones
       </a>
       , which was preserved as a
       <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">
        language isolate
       </a>
       by the barrier of the Pyrenees.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sesars.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="62" data-file-width="190" height="72" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Sesars.svg/220px-Sesars.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Sesars.svg/330px-Sesars.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Sesars.svg/440px-Sesars.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sesars.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Northeast Iberian script from
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huesca_(province)" title="Huesca (province)">
          Huesca
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Iberian Peninsula has always been associated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">
        Ebro
       </a>
       , Ibēros in
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">
        ancient Greek
       </a>
       and Ibērus or Hibērus in
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       . The association was so well known it was hardly necessary to state; for example, Ibēria was the country "this side of the Ibērus" in Strabo.
       <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">
        Pliny
       </a>
       goes so far as to assert that the Greeks had called "the whole of Spain" Hiberia because of the Hiberus River.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The river appears in the
       <a href="/wiki/Ebro_Treaty" title="Ebro Treaty">
        Ebro Treaty
       </a>
       of 226 BC between Rome and Carthage, setting the limit of Carthaginian interest at the Ebro. The fullest description of the treaty, stated in
       <a href="/wiki/Appian" title="Appian">
        Appian
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       uses Ibērus. With reference to this border,
       <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">
        Polybius
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       states that the "native name" is
       <i>
        Ibēr
       </i>
       , apparently the original word, stripped of its Greek or Latin
       <i>
        -os
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        -us
       </i>
       termination.
      </p>
      <p>
       The early range of these natives, which geographers and historians place from today's southern Spain to today's southern France along the Mediterranean coast, is marked by instances of a readable script expressing a yet unknown language, dubbed "
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_language" title="Iberian language">
        Iberian
       </a>
       ." Whether this was the native name or was given to them by the Greeks for their residence on the Ebro remains unknown. Credence in Polybius imposes certain limitations on etymologizing: if the language remains unknown, the meanings of the words, including Iber, must also remain unknown. In modern
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       , the word
       <i>
        ibar
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morris-22">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       means "valley" or "watered meadow", while
       <i>
        ibai
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morris-22">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       means "river", but there is no proof relating the etymology of the Ebro River with these Basque names. In
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">
        Serbia
       </a>
       , there is river
       <a href="/wiki/Ibar_(river)" title="Ibar (river)">
        Ibar
       </a>
       , but there is no proof relating the etymology of the Ebro River with this Serbian river name.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">
        Prehistory
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Prehistory">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Iberia" title="Prehistoric Iberia">
        Prehistoric Iberia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arte_esquem%C3%A1tico-Cig%C3%BCe%C3%B1a.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="844" data-file-width="734" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Arte_esquem%C3%A1tico-Cig%C3%BCe%C3%B1a.png/220px-Arte_esquem%C3%A1tico-Cig%C3%BCe%C3%B1a.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Arte_esquem%C3%A1tico-Cig%C3%BCe%C3%B1a.png/330px-Arte_esquem%C3%A1tico-Cig%C3%BCe%C3%B1a.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Arte_esquem%C3%A1tico-Cig%C3%BCe%C3%B1a.png/440px-Arte_esquem%C3%A1tico-Cig%C3%BCe%C3%B1a.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arte_esquem%C3%A1tico-Cig%C3%BCe%C3%B1a.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Schematic rock art from the Iberian Peninsula.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iberia_Late_Bronze.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="762" data-file-width="924" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Iberia_Late_Bronze.svg/220px-Iberia_Late_Bronze.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Iberia_Late_Bronze.svg/330px-Iberia_Late_Bronze.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Iberia_Late_Bronze.svg/440px-Iberia_Late_Bronze.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iberia_Late_Bronze.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Iberian Late Bronze Age since c. 1300 BC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Palaeolithic">
        Palaeolithic
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Palaeolithic">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Iberian Peninsula has been inhabited for at least 1.2 million years as remains found in the sites in the
       <a href="/wiki/Atapuerca_Mountains" title="Atapuerca Mountains">
        Atapuerca Mountains
       </a>
       demonstrate. Among these sites is the cave of Gran Dolina, where six
       <a href="/wiki/Hominini" title="Hominini">
        hominin
       </a>
       skeletons, dated between 780,000 and one million years ago, were found in 1994. Experts have debated whether these skeletons belong to the species
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">
         Homo erectus
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Homo_heidelbergensis" title="Homo heidelbergensis">
         Homo heidelbergensis
        </a>
       </i>
       , or a new species called
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Homo_antecessor" title="Homo antecessor">
         Homo antecessor
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Around 200,000
       <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">
        BP
       </a>
       , during the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">
        Lower Paleolithic
       </a>
       period, Neanderthals first entered the Iberian Peninsula. Around 70,000 BP, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">
        Middle Paleolithic
       </a>
       period, the last glacial event began and the Neanderthal
       <a href="/wiki/Mousterian" title="Mousterian">
        Mousterian
       </a>
       culture was established. Around 37,000 BP, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">
        Upper Paleolithic
       </a>
       , the Neanderthal
       <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2telperronian" title="Châtelperronian">
        Châtelperronian
       </a>
       cultural period began. Emanating from
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_France" title="Southern France">
        Southern France
       </a>
       , this culture extended into the north of the peninsula. It continued to exist until around 30,000 BP, when Neanderthal man faced extinction.
      </p>
      <p>
       About 40,000 years ago,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_humans" title="Anatomically modern humans">
        anatomically modern humans
       </a>
       entered the Iberian Peninsula from
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_France" title="Southern France">
        Southern France
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adams2010_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Adams2010-23">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Here, this
       <a href="/wiki/Population_genetics" title="Population genetics">
        genetically homogeneous population
       </a>
       (characterized by the
       <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R1#Paragroup_R-M173" title="Haplogroup R1">
        M173 mutation
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Y_chromosome" title="Y chromosome">
        Y chromosome
       </a>
       ), developed the M343 mutation, giving rise to
       <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R1b" title="Haplogroup R1b">
        Haplogroup R1b
       </a>
       , still the most common in modern
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">
        Spanish
       </a>
       males.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the Iberian Peninsula, modern humans developed a series of different cultures, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Aurignacian" title="Aurignacian">
        Aurignacian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gravettian" title="Gravettian">
        Gravettian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Solutrean" title="Solutrean">
        Solutrean
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Magdalenian" title="Magdalenian">
        Magdalenian
       </a>
       cultures, some of them characterized by the complex forms of the
       <a href="/wiki/Art_of_the_Upper_Paleolithic" title="Art of the Upper Paleolithic">
        art of the Upper Paleolithic
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Neolithic">
        Neolithic
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Neolithic">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Europe" title="Neolithic Europe">
        Neolithic expansion
       </a>
       , various
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megalithic" title="Megalithic">
        megalithic
       </a>
       cultures developed in the Iberian Peninsula. An open seas navigation culture from the east Mediterranean, called the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardium_Pottery" title="Cardium Pottery">
        Cardium culture
       </a>
       , also extended its influence to the eastern coasts of the peninsula, possibly as early as the 5th millennium BC. These people may have had some relation to the subsequent development of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">
        Iberian civilization
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Chalcolithic">
        Chalcolithic
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Chalcolithic">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Chalcolithic" title="Chalcolithic">
        Chalcolithic
       </a>
       (c. 3000 BC), a series of complex cultures developed that would give rise to the peninsula's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_civilization" title="First civilization">
        first civilizations
       </a>
       and to extensive exchange networks reaching to the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">
        Middle East
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       . Around 2800 – 2700 BC, the
       <a href="/wiki/Beaker_culture" title="Beaker culture">
        Beaker culture
       </a>
       , which produced the
       <i>
        Maritime Bell Beaker
       </i>
       , probably originated in the vibrant copper-using communities of the
       <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">
        Tagus
       </a>
       estuary in Portugal and spread from there to many parts of western Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-case_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-case-25">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bronze_Age">
        Bronze Age
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bronze Age">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">
        Bronze Age
       </a>
       cultures developed beginning c.1800 BC, when the civilization of
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Millares" title="Los Millares">
        Los Millares
       </a>
       was followed by that of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Argar" title="El Argar">
        El Argar
       </a>
       . From this centre, bronze technology spread to other cultures like the
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_of_Levante" title="Bronze of Levante">
        Bronze of Levante
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/South-Western_Iberian_Bronze" title="South-Western Iberian Bronze">
        South-Western Iberian Bronze
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Cogotas" title="Las Cogotas">
        Las Cogotas
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the Late Bronze Age, the urban civilisation of
       <a href="/wiki/Tartessos" title="Tartessos">
        Tartessos
       </a>
       developed in the area of modern western
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       , characterized by
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
        Phoenician
       </a>
       influence and using the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Paleohispanic_script" title="Southwest Paleohispanic script">
        Southwest Paleohispanic script
       </a>
       for its
       <a href="/wiki/Tartessian_language" title="Tartessian language">
        Tartessian language
       </a>
       , not related to the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_language" title="Iberian language">
        Iberian language
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Early in the first millennium BC, several waves of Pre-Celts and
       <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">
        Celts
       </a>
       migrated from
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
        Central Europe
       </a>
       , thus partially changing the peninsula's ethnic landscape to
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European-speaking
       </a>
       in its northern and western regions. In Northwestern Iberia (modern Northern Portugal, Asturias and Galicia), a Celtic culture developed, the
       <a href="/wiki/Castro_culture" title="Castro culture">
        Castro culture
       </a>
       , with a large number of hill forts and some fortified cities.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Proto-history">
        Proto-history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Proto-history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">
        Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       By the
       <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">
        Iron Age
       </a>
       , starting in the 7th century BC, the Iberian Peninsula consisted of complex agrarian and urban civilizations, either Pre-Celtic or Celtic (such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">
        Lusitanians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Celtiberians" title="Celtiberians">
        Celtiberians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gallaeci" title="Gallaeci">
        Gallaeci
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Astures" title="Astures">
        Astures
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">
        Celtici
       </a>
       and others), the cultures of the Iberians in the eastern and southern zones and the cultures of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aquitanian_language" title="Aquitanian language">
        Aquitanian
       </a>
       in the western portion of the Pyrenees.
      </p>
      <p>
       The seafaring Phoenicians,
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
        Greeks
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">
        Carthaginians
       </a>
       successively settled along the Mediterranean coast and founded trading colonies there over a period of several centuries. Around 1100 BC, Phoenician merchants founded the trading colony of Gadir or Gades (modern day
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">
        Cádiz
       </a>
       ) near
       <a href="/wiki/Tartessos" title="Tartessos">
        Tartessos
       </a>
       . In the 8th century BC, the first
       <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity#Greek_colonies" title="Colonies in antiquity">
        Greek colonies
       </a>
       , such as Emporion (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Emp%C3%BAries" title="Empúries">
        Empúries
       </a>
       ), were founded along the Mediterranean coast on the east, leaving the south coast to the Phoenicians. The Greeks coined the name Iberia, after the river Iber (Ebro). In the sixth century BC, the Carthaginians arrived in the peninsula while struggling with the Greeks for control of the Western Mediterranean. Their most important colony was Carthago Nova (modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Spain" title="Cartagena, Spain">
        Cartagena, Spain
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_rule">
        Roman rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Roman rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">
        Lusitania
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Conquista_Hispania.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="950" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Conquista_Hispania.svg/220px-Conquista_Hispania.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Conquista_Hispania.svg/330px-Conquista_Hispania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Conquista_Hispania.svg/440px-Conquista_Hispania.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Conquista_Hispania.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Roman conquest: 220 BC - 19 BC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 218 BC, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">
        Second Punic War
       </a>
       against the Carthaginians, the first
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
        Roman
       </a>
       troops invaded the Iberian Peninsula; however, it was not until the reign of
       <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">
        Augustus
       </a>
       that it was annexed after two centuries of war with the Celtic and Iberian tribes and the Phoenician, Greek and Carthaginian colonies. The result was the creation of the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       . It was divided into
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Ulterior" title="Hispania Ulterior">
        Hispania Ulterior
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Citerior" title="Hispania Citerior">
        Hispania Citerior
       </a>
       during the late
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Roman Republic
       </a>
       , and during the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , it was divided into
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Tarraconensis" title="Hispania Tarraconensis">
        Hispania Tarraconensis
       </a>
       in the northeast,
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Baetica" title="Hispania Baetica">
        Hispania Baetica
       </a>
       in the south and
       <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">
        Lusitania
       </a>
       in the southwest.
      </p>
      <p>
       Hispania supplied the Roman Empire with silver, food, olive oil, wine, and metal. The emperors
       <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">
        Trajan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">
        Hadrian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius" title="Marcus Aurelius">
        Marcus Aurelius
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">
        Theodosius I
       </a>
       , the philosopher
       <a href="/wiki/Seneca_the_Younger" title="Seneca the Younger">
        Seneca the Younger
       </a>
       , and the poets
       <a href="/wiki/Martial" title="Martial">
        Martial
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lucan" title="Lucan">
        Lucan
       </a>
       were born from families living on the Iberian Peninsula.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Germanic_kingdoms">
        Germanic kingdoms
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Germanic kingdoms">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
        Visigothic Kingdom
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spania" title="Spania">
        Spania
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hispania_560_AD.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2500" data-file-width="2500" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Hispania_560_AD.PNG/220px-Hispania_560_AD.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Hispania_560_AD.PNG/330px-Hispania_560_AD.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Hispania_560_AD.PNG/440px-Hispania_560_AD.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hispania_560_AD.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Germanic and Byzantine rule c.560
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the early fifth century,
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">
        Germanic peoples
       </a>
       invaded the peninsula, namely the
       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">
        Suebi
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Silingi" title="Silingi">
        Silingi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hasdingi" title="Hasdingi">
        Hasdingi
       </a>
       ) and their allies, the
       <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">
        Alans
       </a>
       . Only the kingdom of the Suebi (
       <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">
        Quadi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Marcomanni" title="Marcomanni">
        Marcomanni
       </a>
       ) would endure after the arrival of another wave of Germanic invaders, the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       , who conquered all of the Iberian Peninsula and expelled or partially integrated the Vandals and the Alans. The Visigoths eventually conquered the Suebi kingdom and its capital city, Bracara (modern day
       <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">
        Braga
       </a>
       ), in 584–585. They would also conquer the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">
        province
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       (552–624) of
       <a href="/wiki/Spania" title="Spania">
        Spania
       </a>
       in the south of the peninsula and the
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
        Balearic Islands
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_Caliphate">
        Islamic Caliphate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Islamic Caliphate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Al-Andalus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Spain" title="Islam in Spain">
        Islam in Spain
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Portugal" title="Islam in Portugal">
        Islam in Portugal
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al_Andalus_%26_Christian_Kingdoms.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="497" data-file-width="670" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Al_Andalus_%26_Christian_Kingdoms.png/220px-Al_Andalus_%26_Christian_Kingdoms.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Al_Andalus_%26_Christian_Kingdoms.png/330px-Al_Andalus_%26_Christian_Kingdoms.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Al_Andalus_%26_Christian_Kingdoms.png/440px-Al_Andalus_%26_Christian_Kingdoms.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al_Andalus_%26_Christian_Kingdoms.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Islamic rule:
         <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
          al-Andalus
         </a>
         c.1000
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 711, a Muslim army invaded the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        Visigothic Kingdom in Hispania
       </a>
       . Under
       <a href="/wiki/Tariq_ibn_Ziyad" title="Tariq ibn Ziyad">
        Tariq ibn Ziyad
       </a>
       , the Islamic army landed at Gibraltar and, in an eight-year campaign, occupied all except the northern kingdoms of the Iberian Peninsula in the
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">
        Umayyad conquest of Hispania
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Al-Andalus
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       :
       <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
        الإندلس
       </span>
       ‎, tr.
       <i>
        al-ʾAndalūs
       </i>
       , possibly "Land of the Vandals"),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Samsó1998_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Samsó1998-27">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is the Arabic name given to what is today southern Spain by its
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
        Muslim
       </a>
       Berber and Arab occupiers.
      </p>
      <p>
       From the 8th–15th centuries, only the southern part of the Iberian Peninsula was incorporated into the Islamic world and became a center of culture and learning, especially during the
       <a href="/wiki/Caliphate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Caliphate of Córdoba">
        Caliphate of Córdoba
       </a>
       , which reached its height under the rule of
       <a href="/wiki/Abd-ar-Rahman_III" title="Abd-ar-Rahman III">
        Abd-ar-Rahman III
       </a>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . The Muslims, who were initially
       <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">
        Arabs
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">
        Berbers
       </a>
       , included some local converts, the so-called
       <a href="/wiki/Muladi" title="Muladi">
        Muladi
       </a>
       . The Muslims were referred to by the generic name,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">
         Moors
        </a>
       </i>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        Reconquista
       </a>
       gained momentum on c. 718, when the Christian Asturians opposed the Moors, the southern march to push out the Muslims continued for three hundred years, so for another four hundred years, only the southern part of the Iberian Peninsula was transformed into a Romance-speaking and Arabic-speaking Muslim land, along with pockets of a large minority of Arabic-speaking
       <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">
        Sephardi Jews
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reconquest">
        Reconquest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reconquest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        Reconquista
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many of the ousted
       <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">
        Gothic
       </a>
       nobles took refuge in the unconquered north
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">
        Kingdom of Asturias
       </a>
       . From there, they aimed to reconquer their lands from the Moors; this war of reconquest is known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        Reconquista
       </a>
       . Christian and Muslim kingdoms fought and allied among themselves. The Muslim
       <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">
        taifa
       </a>
       kings competed in patronage of the arts, the
       <a href="/wiki/Camino_de_Santiago" title="Camino de Santiago">
        Camino de Santiago
       </a>
       attracted pilgrims from all Western Europe, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_age_of_Jewish_culture_in_Spain" title="Golden age of Jewish culture in Spain">
        Jewish population
       </a>
       set the basis of Sephardi culture.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the Middle Ages, the peninsula housed many small states including the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">
        Kingdom of Castile
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">
        Crown of Aragon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">
        Kingdom of Navarre
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">
        Kingdom of León
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">
        Kingdom of Portugal
       </a>
       . The peninsula was part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">
        Almohad Caliphate
       </a>
       until they were finally uprooted. The last major Muslim stronghold was
       <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
        Granada
       </a>
       , which was conquered by a combined Castilian and Aragonese force in 1492. Muslims and Jews throughout the period were variously tolerated or shown intolerance in different Christian kingdoms. However, after the
       <a href="/wiki/Granada_War#Last_stand_at_Granada" title="Granada War">
        fall of Granada
       </a>
       , all Muslims and Jews were ordered to convert to Christianity or face expulsion. Many Jews and Muslims fled to
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       , while others publicly converted to Christianity and became known respectively as
       <a href="/wiki/Marrano" title="Marrano">
        Marranos
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Morisco" title="Morisco">
        Moriscos
       </a>
       . However, many of these continued to practice their religion in secret. The Moriscos revolted several times and were ultimately
       <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos">
        forcibly expelled
       </a>
       from Spain in the early 17th century.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carte_historique_des_Royaumes_d%27Espagne_et_Portugal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2313" data-file-width="2795" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Carte_historique_des_Royaumes_d%27Espagne_et_Portugal.jpg/220px-Carte_historique_des_Royaumes_d%27Espagne_et_Portugal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Carte_historique_des_Royaumes_d%27Espagne_et_Portugal.jpg/330px-Carte_historique_des_Royaumes_d%27Espagne_et_Portugal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Carte_historique_des_Royaumes_d%27Espagne_et_Portugal.jpg/440px-Carte_historique_des_Royaumes_d%27Espagne_et_Portugal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carte_historique_des_Royaumes_d%27Espagne_et_Portugal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Spain and Portugal,
         <i>
          Atlas historique
         </i>
         , dated approximately 1705–1739, of H.A. Chatelain.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-reconquest">
        Post-reconquest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Post-reconquest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Andorra" title="History of Andorra">
        History of Andorra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Gibraltar" title="History of Gibraltar">
        History of Gibraltar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal" title="History of Portugal">
        History of Portugal
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Spain" title="History of Spain">
        History of Spain
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The small states gradually amalgamated over time, with the exception of Portugal, even if for a brief period (1580–1640) the whole peninsula was united politically under the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">
        Iberian Union
       </a>
       . After that point, the modern position was reached and the peninsula now consists of the countries of Spain and Portugal (excluding their islands—the Portuguese
       <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">
        Azores
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">
        Madeira
       </a>
       and the Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
        Canary Islands
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
        Balearic Islands
       </a>
       ; and the Spanish
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave">
        exclaves
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">
        Ceuta
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">
        Melilla
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">
        Andorra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_Cerdagne" title="French Cerdagne">
        French Cerdagne
       </a>
       and Gibraltar.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iberian_Peninsula_antique_map.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="2096" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Iberian_Peninsula_antique_map.jpg/220px-Iberian_Peninsula_antique_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Iberian_Peninsula_antique_map.jpg/330px-Iberian_Peninsula_antique_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Iberian_Peninsula_antique_map.jpg/440px-Iberian_Peninsula_antique_map.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iberian_Peninsula_antique_map.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An 18th-century map of the peninsula depicting various topographical features of the land, as published in Robert Wilkinson's
         <i>
          General Atlas
         </i>
         , circa 1794.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_geology">
        Geography and geology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Geography and geology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Portugal" title="Geography of Portugal">
        Geography of Portugal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Spain" title="Geography of Spain">
        Geography of Spain
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Iberian Peninsula is the westernmost of the three major southern European peninsulas—the Iberian,
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">
        Italian
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">
        Balkan
       </a>
       . It is bordered on the southeast and east by the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       , and on the north, west, and southwest by the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       . The Pyrenees mountains are situated along the northeast edge of the peninsula, where it adjoins the rest of Europe. Its southern tip is very close to the northwest coast of Africa, separated from it by the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Iberian Peninsula extends from the southernmost extremity at
       <a href="/wiki/Punta_de_Tarifa" title="Punta de Tarifa">
        Punta de Tarifa
       </a>
       (
       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;params=36_00_15_N_5_36_37_W_">
         <span class="geo-default">
          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           <span class="latitude">
            36°00′15″N
           </span>
           <span class="longitude">
            5°36′37″W
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          ﻿ / ﻿
         </span>
         <span class="geo-nondefault">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           36.00417°N 5.61028°W
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
           ﻿ /
           <span class="geo">
            36.00417; -5.61028
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </span>
       ) to the northernmost extremity at
       <a href="/wiki/Punta_de_Estaca_de_Bares" title="Punta de Estaca de Bares">
        Punta de Estaca de Bares
       </a>
       (
       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;params=43_47_38_N_7_41_17_W_">
         <span class="geo-default">
          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           <span class="latitude">
            43°47′38″N
           </span>
           <span class="longitude">
            7°41′17″W
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          ﻿ / ﻿
         </span>
         <span class="geo-nondefault">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           43.79389°N 7.68806°W
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
           ﻿ /
           <span class="geo">
            43.79389; -7.68806
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </span>
       ) over a distance between lines of latitude of about 865 km (537 mi) based on a
       <a href="/wiki/Latitude#Degree_length" title="Latitude">
        degree length
       </a>
       of 111 km (69 mi) per degree, and from the westernmost extremity at
       <a href="/wiki/Cabo_da_Roca" title="Cabo da Roca">
        Cabo da Roca
       </a>
       (
       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;params=38_46_51_N_9_29_54_W_">
         <span class="geo-default">
          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           <span class="latitude">
            38°46′51″N
           </span>
           <span class="longitude">
            9°29′54″W
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          ﻿ / ﻿
         </span>
         <span class="geo-nondefault">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           38.78083°N 9.49833°W
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
           ﻿ /
           <span class="geo">
            38.78083; -9.49833
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </span>
       ) to the easternmost extremity at
       <a href="/wiki/Cap_de_Creus" title="Cap de Creus">
        Cap de Creus
       </a>
       (
       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;params=42_19_09_N_3_19_19_E_">
         <span class="geo-default">
          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           <span class="latitude">
            42°19′09″N
           </span>
           <span class="longitude">
            3°19′19″E
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          ﻿ / ﻿
         </span>
         <span class="geo-nondefault">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           42.31917°N 3.32194°E
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
           ﻿ /
           <span class="geo">
            42.31917; 3.32194
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </span>
       ) over a distance between lines of longitude at
       <a href="/wiki/40th_parallel_north" title="40th parallel north">
        40° N latitude
       </a>
       of about 1,155 km (718 mi) based on an estimated degree length of about 90 km (56 mi) for that latitude. The irregular, roughly octagonal shape of the peninsula contained within this spherical
       <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(geography)" title="Quadrangle (geography)">
        quadrangle
       </a>
       was compared to an ox-hide by the geographer
       <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">
        Strabo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       About three quarters of that rough octagon is the
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Spain#The_Inner_Plateau_and_associated_mountains" title="Geography of Spain">
        Meseta Central
       </a>
       , a vast plateau ranging from 610 to 760 m in altitude.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is located approximately in the centre, staggered slightly to the east and tilted slightly toward the west (the conventional centre of the Iberian Peninsula has long been considered
       <a href="/wiki/Getafe" title="Getafe">
        Getafe
       </a>
       just south of
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
        Madrid
       </a>
       ). It is ringed by mountains and contains the sources of most of the rivers, which find their way through gaps in the mountain barriers on all sides.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Coastline">
        Coastline
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Coastline">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The coastline of the Iberian Peninsula is 3,313 km (2,059 mi), 1,660 km (1,030 mi) on the Mediterranean side and 1,653 km (1,027 mi) on the Atlantic side.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The coast has been inundated over time, with sea levels having risen from a minimum of 115–120 m (377–394 ft) lower than today at the
       <a href="/wiki/Last_Glacial_Maximum" title="Last Glacial Maximum">
        Last Glacial Maximum
       </a>
       (LGM) to its current level at 4,000 years
       <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">
        BP
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The coastal shelf created by sedimentation during that time remains below the surface; however, it was never very extensive on the Atlantic side, as the continental shelf drops rather steeply into the depths. An estimated 700 km (430 mi) length of Atlantic shelf is only 10–65 km (6.2–40.4 mi) wide. At the 500 m (1,600 ft)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isobath" title="Isobath">
        isobath
       </a>
       , on the edge, the shelf drops off to 1,000 m (3,300 ft).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The submarine topography of the coastal waters of the Iberian Peninsula has been studied extensively in the process of drilling for oil. Ultimately, the shelf drops into the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">
        Bay of Biscay
       </a>
       on the north (an abyss), the Iberian abyssal plain at 4,800 m (15,700 ft) on the west, and Tagus abyssal plain to the south. In the north, between the continental shelf and the abyss, is an extension called the Galicia Bank, a plateau that also contains the Porto, Vigo, and Vasco da Gama
       <a href="/wiki/Seamount" title="Seamount">
        seamounts
       </a>
       , which form the Galicia interior basin. The southern border of these features is marked by
       <a href="/wiki/Nazar%C3%A9_Canyon" title="Nazaré Canyon">
        Nazaré Canyon
       </a>
       , which splits the continental shelf and leads directly into the abyss.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rivers">
        Rivers
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rivers">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Portugal" title="List of rivers of Portugal">
        List of rivers of Portugal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Spain" title="List of rivers of Spain">
        List of rivers of Spain
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rios_peninsula_Iberica-es.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2347" data-file-width="3056" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Rios_peninsula_Iberica-es.png/220px-Rios_peninsula_Iberica-es.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Rios_peninsula_Iberica-es.png/330px-Rios_peninsula_Iberica-es.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Rios_peninsula_Iberica-es.png/440px-Rios_peninsula_Iberica-es.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rios_peninsula_Iberica-es.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Major rivers of the Iberian Peninsula:
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minho_River" title="Minho River">
          Miño / Minho
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">
          Duero / Douro
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">
          Tajo / Tejo
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Guadiana" title="Guadiana">
          Guadiana
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">
          Guadalquivir
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Segura" title="Segura">
          Segura
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAcar" title="Júcar">
          Júcar / Xúquer
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">
          Ebro / Ebre
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The major rivers flow through the wide valleys between the mountain systems. These are the
       <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">
        Ebro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">
        Douro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">
        Tagus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guadiana" title="Guadiana">
        Guadiana
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">
        Guadalquivir
       </a>
       . All rivers in the Iberian Peninsula are subject to seasonal variations in flow.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Tagus is the longest river on the peninsula and, like the Douro, flows westwards with its lower course in Portugal. The Guadiana river bends southwards and forms the border between Spain and Portugal in the last stretch of its course.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mountains">
        Mountains
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Mountains">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geological_units_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula_EN.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="542" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Geological_units_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula_EN.svg/220px-Geological_units_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula_EN.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Geological_units_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula_EN.svg/330px-Geological_units_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula_EN.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Geological_units_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula_EN.svg/440px-Geological_units_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula_EN.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geological_units_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula_EN.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Major Geologic Units of the Iberian Peninsula
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The terrain of the Iberian Peninsula is largely
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountainous" title="Mountainous">
        mountainous
       </a>
       . The major mountain systems are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">
         Pyrenees
        </a>
        and their foothills, the
        <a href="/wiki/Pre-Pyrenees" title="Pre-Pyrenees">
         Pre-Pyrenees
        </a>
        , crossing the isthmus of the peninsula so completely as to allow no passage except by mountain road, trail, coastal road or tunnel.
        <a href="/wiki/Aneto" title="Aneto">
         Aneto
        </a>
        in the
        <a href="/wiki/Maladeta" title="Maladeta">
         Maladeta
        </a>
        massif, at 3,404 m, is the highest point
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Mountains" title="Cantabrian Mountains">
         Cantabrian Mountains
        </a>
        along the northern coast with the massive
        <a href="/wiki/Picos_de_Europa" title="Picos de Europa">
         Picos de Europa
        </a>
        .
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torre_de_Cerredo" title="Torre de Cerredo">
         Torre de Cerredo
        </a>
        , at 2,648 m, is the highest point
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Galician_Massif" title="Galician Massif">
         Galicia/Trás-os-Montes Massif
        </a>
        in the Northwest is made up of very old heavily eroded rocks.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
         <a href="#cite_note-33">
          [31]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pena_Trevinca" title="Pena Trevinca">
         Pena Trevinca
        </a>
        , at 2,127 m, is the highest point
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Ib%C3%A9rico" title="Sistema Ibérico">
         Sistema Ibérico
        </a>
        , a complex system at the heart of the Peninsula, in its central/eastern region. It contains a great number of ranges and divides the watershed of the Tagus, Douro and Ebro rivers.
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moncayo" title="Moncayo">
         Moncayo
        </a>
        , at 2,313 m, is the highest point
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Central" title="Sistema Central">
         Sistema Central
        </a>
        , dividing the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberian_Plateau" title="Iberian Plateau">
         Iberian Plateau
        </a>
        into a northern and a southern half and stretching into Portugal (where the highest point of
        <a href="/wiki/Continental_Portugal" title="Continental Portugal">
         Continental Portugal
        </a>
        (1,993 m) is located in the
        <a href="/wiki/Serra_da_Estrela" title="Serra da Estrela">
         Serra da Estrela
        </a>
        ).
        <a href="/wiki/Pico_Almanzor" title="Pico Almanzor">
         Pico Almanzor
        </a>
        in the
        <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Gredos" title="Sierra de Gredos">
         Sierra de Gredos
        </a>
        is the highest point, at 2,592 m
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Montes_de_Toledo" title="Montes de Toledo">
         Montes de Toledo
        </a>
        , which also stretches into Portugal from the
        <a href="/wiki/La_Mancha" title="La Mancha">
