         La Mancha
        </a>
        natural region at the eastern end. Its highest point, at 1,603 m, is
        <a href="/wiki/La_Villuerca" title="La Villuerca">
         La Villuerca
        </a>
        in the
        <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Villuercas" title="Sierra de Villuercas">
         Sierra de Villuercas
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">
         Extremadura
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Morena" title="Sierra Morena">
         Sierra Morena
        </a>
        , which divides the watershed of the Guadiana and Guadalquivir rivers. At 1,332 m,
        <a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%B1uela" title="Bañuela">
         Bañuela
        </a>
        is the highest point
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Baetic_System" title="Baetic System">
         Baetic System
        </a>
        , which stretches between
        <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">
         Cádiz
        </a>
        and Gibraltar and northeast towards
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alicante_Province" title="Alicante Province">
         Alicante Province
        </a>
        . It is divided into three subsystems:
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Prebaetic_System" title="Prebaetic System">
           Prebaetic System
          </a>
          , which begins west of the
          <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Sur_de_Ja%C3%A9n" title="Sierra Sur de Jaén">
           Sierra Sur de Jaén
          </a>
          , reaching the
          <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
           Mediterranean Sea
          </a>
          shores in
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alicante_Province" title="Alicante Province">
           Alicante Province
          </a>
          .
          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Sagra_(peak)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Sagra (peak) (page does not exist)">
           La Sagra
          </a>
          is the highest point at 2,382 m.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Subbaetic_System" title="Subbaetic System">
           Subbaetic System
          </a>
          , which is in a central position within the Baetic Systems, stretching from
          <a href="/wiki/Cape_Trafalgar" title="Cape Trafalgar">
           Cape Trafalgar
          </a>
          in
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_Province" title="Cádiz Province">
           Cádiz Province
          </a>
          across Andalusia to the
          <a href="/wiki/Region_of_Murcia" title="Region of Murcia">
           Region of Murcia
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
           <a href="#cite_note-34">
            [32]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The highest point, at 2,027 m (6,650 ft), is Peña de la Cruz in
          <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Arana" title="Sierra Arana">
           Sierra Arana
          </a>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Penibaetic_System" title="Penibaetic System">
           Penibaetic System
          </a>
          , located in the far southeastern area stretching between Gibraltar across the Mediterranean coastal Andalusian provinces. It includes the highest point in the peninsula, the 3,478 m high
          <a href="/wiki/Mulhac%C3%A9n" title="Mulhacén">
           Mulhacén
          </a>
          in the
          <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(Spain)" title="Sierra Nevada (Spain)">
           Sierra Nevada
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
           <a href="#cite_note-35">
            [33]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">
        Geology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Geology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Geology of the Iberian Peninsula">
        Geology of the Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Iberian Peninsula contains rocks of every geological period from the
       <a href="/wiki/Ediacaran" title="Ediacaran">
        Ediacaran
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">
        Recent
       </a>
       , and almost every kind of rock is represented. World-class
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mineral_deposit" title="Mineral deposit">
        mineral deposits
       </a>
       can also be found there. The core of the Iberian Peninsula consists of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hercynian" title="Hercynian">
        Hercynian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Craton" title="Craton">
        cratonic
       </a>
       block known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberian_Massif" title="Iberian Massif">
        Iberian Massif
       </a>
       . On the northeast, this is bounded by the Pyrenean fold belt, and on the southeast it is bounded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Baetic_System" title="Baetic System">
        Baetic System
       </a>
       . These twofold chains are part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_the_Alps" title="Geology of the Alps">
        Alpine belt
       </a>
       . To the west, the peninsula is delimited by the continental boundary formed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">
        magma
       </a>
       -poor opening of the Atlantic Ocean. The Hercynian Foldbelt is mostly buried by Mesozoic and Tertiary cover rocks to the east, but nevertheless outcrops through the
       <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Ib%C3%A9rico" title="Sistema Ibérico">
        Sistema Ibérico
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Mediterranean_System" title="Catalan Mediterranean System">
        Catalan Mediterranean System
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Portugal" title="Climate of Portugal">
        Climate of Portugal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Spain" title="Climate of Spain">
        Climate of Spain
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Iberian peninsula has two dominant climate types. One of these is the
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">
        oceanic climate
       </a>
       seen in the Atlantic coastal region resulting in evenly temperatures with relatively cool summers. However, most of Portugal and Spain have a
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">
        mediterranean climate
       </a>
       with various precipitation and temperatures depending on latitude and position versus the sea. There are also more localized
       <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">
        semi-arid climates
       </a>
       in central Spain, with temperatures resembling a more continental mediterranean climate. In other extreme cases highland alpine climates such as in
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(Spain)" title="Sierra Nevada (Spain)">
        Sierra Nevada
       </a>
       and areas with extremely low precitipation and
       <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">
        desert climates
       </a>
       nor
       <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">
        semi-arid climates
       </a>
       such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Almer%C3%ADa" title="Almería">
        Almería
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       area,
       <a href="/wiki/Murcia" title="Murcia">
        Murcia
       </a>
       area and southern
       <a href="/wiki/Alicante" title="Alicante">
        Alicante
       </a>
       area. In the Spanish interior the hottest temperatures in Europe are found, with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Andalusia" title="Córdoba, Andalusia">
        Córdoba
       </a>
       averaging around 37 °C (99 °F) in July.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Spanish mediterranean coast usually averages around 30 °C (86 °F) in summer. In sharp contrast
       <a href="/wiki/A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="A Coruña">
        A Coruña
       </a>
       at the northern tip of
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       has a summer daytime high average at just below 23 °C (73 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This cool and wet summer climate is replicated throughout most of the northern coastline. Winter temperatures are more consistent throughout the peninsula, although frosts are common in the Spanish interior, even though daytime highs are usually above the freezing point. In Portugal, the warmest winters of the country are found in the area of
       <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">
        Algarve
       </a>
       , very similar to the ones from
       <a href="/wiki/Huelva" title="Huelva">
        Huelva
       </a>
       in Spain, while most of the Portuguese Atlantic coast has fresh and humid winters, similar to
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin: 1em auto 1em auto; width: 60%; font-size: 95%">

      <p>
       The main metropolitan areas of the Iberian Peninsula are
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid_metropolitan_area" title="Madrid metropolitan area">
        Madrid
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_metropolitan_area" title="Barcelona metropolitan area">
        Barcelona
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisbon_Metropolitan_Area" title="Lisbon Metropolitan Area">
        Lisbon
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Valencia metropolitan area (page does not exist)">
        Valencia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Metropolitan_Area_of_Porto" title="Greater Metropolitan Area of Porto">
        Porto
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Seville_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Seville metropolitan area (page does not exist)">
        Seville
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bilbao_metropolitan_area" title="Bilbao metropolitan area">
        Bilbao
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1vado_(intermunicipal_community)" title="Cávado (intermunicipal community)">
        Braga
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=M%C3%A1laga_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Málaga metropolitan area (page does not exist)">
        Málaga
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Central_Asturias_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Central Asturias metropolitan area (page does not exist)">
        Central Asturias
       </a>
       (Gijón-Oviedo-Avilés),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alicante-Elche-Elda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alicante-Elche-Elda (page does not exist)">
        Alicante-Elche
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Murcia_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Murcia metropolitan area (page does not exist)">
        Murcia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">
        Coimbra
       </a>
       .
      </p>

          20
         </b>
        </td>
        <td align="left">
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
           Granada
          </a>
         </b>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
          Andalusia
         </a>
         , Spain
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         237,540
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <p>
       Various other notable cities are also present on the peninsula, such as:
       <a href="/wiki/Elche" title="Elche">
        Elche
       </a>
       (230,354),
       <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">
        Oviedo
       </a>
       (225,973),
       <a href="/wiki/Badalona" title="Badalona">
        Badalona
       </a>
       (220,977) and
       <a href="/wiki/Terrassa" title="Terrassa">
        Terrassa
       </a>
       (215 678) in Spain; and
       <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">
        Braga
       </a>
       (181,874),
       <a href="/wiki/Amadora" title="Amadora">
        Amadora
       </a>
       (175,558),
       <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">
        Coimbra
       </a>
       (102,455) and
       <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal" title="Setúbal">
        Setúbal
       </a>
       (90,640) in Portugal.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">
        Ecology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ecology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Forests">
        Forests
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Forests">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Forests_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Forests of the Iberian Peninsula">
        Forests of the Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The woodlands of the Iberian Peninsula are distinct
       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">
        ecosystems
       </a>
       . Although the various regions are each characterized by distinct vegetation, there are some similarities across the peninsula.
      </p>
      <p>
       While the borders between these regions are not clearly defined, there is a mutual influence that makes it very hard to establish boundaries and some species find their optimal habitat in the intermediate areas.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="East_Atlantic_flyway">
        East Atlantic flyway
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: East Atlantic flyway">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Iberian Peninsula in an important stopover on the East Atlantic
       <a href="/wiki/Flyway" title="Flyway">
        flyway
       </a>
       for birds migrating from northern Europe to Africa. For example,
       <a href="/wiki/Curlew_sandpiper" title="Curlew sandpiper">
        curlew sandpipers
       </a>
       rest in the region of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Bay of Cádiz">
        Bay of Cádiz
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to the birds migrating through, some seven million wading birds from the north spend the winter in the estuaries and wetlands of the Iberian Peninsula, mainly at locations on the Atlantic coast. In
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADa_de_Arousa" title="Ría de Arousa">
        Ría de Arousa
       </a>
       (a home of
       <a href="/wiki/Grey_plover" title="Grey plover">
        grey plover
       </a>
       ), Ria de
       <a href="/wiki/Ortigueira" title="Ortigueira">
        Ortigueira
       </a>
       , Ria de Corme and Ria de Laxe. In Portugal, the
       <a href="/wiki/Aveiro_Lagoon" title="Aveiro Lagoon">
        Aveiro Lagoon
       </a>
       hosts
       <a href="/wiki/Avocet" title="Avocet">
        <i>
         Recurvirostra avosetta
        </i>
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Common_ringed_plover" title="Common ringed plover">
        common ringed plover
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grey_plover" title="Grey plover">
        grey plover
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Little_stint" title="Little stint">
        little stint
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Ribatejo_Province" title="Ribatejo Province">
        Ribatejo Province
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">
        Tagus
       </a>
       supports
       <a href="/wiki/Avocet" title="Avocet">
        <i>
         Recurvirostra arosetta
        </i>
       </a>
       , grey plover,
       <a href="/wiki/Dunlin" title="Dunlin">
        dunlin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bar-tailed_godwit" title="Bar-tailed godwit">
        bar-tailed godwit
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Common_redshank" title="Common redshank">
        common redshank
       </a>
       . In the
       <a href="/wiki/Sado_River" title="Sado River">
        Sado Estuary
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Dunlin" title="Dunlin">
        dunlin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_curlew" title="Eurasian curlew">
        Eurasian curlew
       </a>
       , grey plover and
       <a href="/wiki/Common_redshank" title="Common redshank">
        common redshank
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">
        Algarve
       </a>
       hosts
       <a href="/wiki/Red_knot" title="Red knot">
        red knot
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_greenshank" title="Common greenshank">
        common greenshank
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Turnstone" title="Turnstone">
        turnstone
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir_Marshes" title="Guadalquivir Marshes">
        Guadalquivir Marshes
       </a>
       region of
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       and the Salinas de
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">
        Cádiz
       </a>
       are especially rich in wintering wading birds:
       <a href="/wiki/Kentish_plover" title="Kentish plover">
        Kentish plover
       </a>
       , common ringed plover,
       <a href="/wiki/Sanderling" title="Sanderling">
        sanderling
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Black-tailed_godwit" title="Black-tailed godwit">
        black-tailed godwit
       </a>
       in addition to the others. And finally, the Ebro delta is home to all the species mentioned above.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Iberia" title="Languages of Iberia">
        Languages of Iberia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Andorra" title="Languages of Andorra">
        Languages of Andorra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Gibraltar" title="Languages of Gibraltar">
        Languages of Gibraltar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Spain" title="Languages of Spain">
        Languages of Spain
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Portugal" title="Languages of Portugal">
        Languages of Portugal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       With the sole exception of
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       , which is of
       <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">
        unknown origin
       </a>
       , all modern Iberian languages descend from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       and belong to the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">
        Western Romance languages
       </a>
       . Throughout history (and pre-history), many different languages have been spoken in the Iberian Peninsula, contributing to the formation and differentiation of the contemporaneous languages of Iberia; however, most of them have become extinct or fallen into disuse. Basque is the only
       <a href="/wiki/Pre-Indo-European_languages" title="Pre-Indo-European languages">
        non-Indo-European surviving language
       </a>
       in Iberia and Western Europe.
      </p>
      <p>
       In modern times, Spanish (cf. 30 to 40 million speakers),
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       (cf. around 10 million speakers),
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       (cf. around 9 million speakers),
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       (cf. around 3 million speakers) and
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       (cf. around 1 million speakers)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       are the most widely spoken languages in the Iberian Peninsula. Spanish and Portuguese have expanded beyond Iberia to the rest of world, becoming
       <a href="/wiki/World_language" title="World language">
        global languages
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iberian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Major industries include mining, tourism, small farms, and fishing. Because the coast is so long, fishing is popular, especially sardines, tuna, cod and anchovies. Most of the mining happens in the Pyrenees mountains; iron, gold, coal, valuable minerals—such as lead, silver, zinc, and salt—are all mined.
      </p>

             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">

              </a>
             </span>
            </li>
            <li>
             <small>

             </small>
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
               [iˈβɛɾia; -ˈbɛ-]
              </a>
             </span>
            </li>
            <li>
             <small>

               [iˈβɛɾiɔ; -ˈbɛʀi-]

            </li>

          </li>

        <li id="cite_note-30">

          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-30">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          These figures sum the figures given in the Wikipedia articles on the geography of Spain and Portugal. Most figures from Internet sources on Spain and Portugal include the coastlines of the islands owned by each country and thus are not a reliable guide to the coastline of the peninsula. Moreover, the length of a coastline may vary significantly depending on where and how it is measured.

        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=IberiaNature%3A+A+guide+to+the+environment%2C+climate%2C+wildlife%2C+geography+and+nature+of+Spain&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.aulast=Loyd&amp;rft.aufirst=Nick&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.iberianature.com&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AIberian+Peninsula">
         <span style="display:none;">
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <cite class="citation web">
         Silva, Luís Fraga de.
         <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20081006160601/http://www.arqueotavira.com/Mapas/Iberia/Populi.htm" rel="nofollow">
          "Ethnologic Map of Pre-Roman Iberia (circa 200 B.C.). NEW VERSION #10"
         </a>
         (in English, Portuguese, and Latin). Associação Campo Arqueológico de Tavira, Tavira, Portugal. Archived from
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.arqueotavira.com/Mapas/Iberia/Populi.htm" rel="nofollow">
          the original
         </a>
         on 6 October 2008
         <span class="reference-accessdate">

          <span class="nowrap">
           4 December
          </span>

        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Ethnologic+Map+of+Pre-Roman+Iberia+%28circa+200+B.C.%29.+NEW+VERSION+%2310&amp;rft.pub=Associa%C3%A7%C3%A3o+Campo+Arqueol%C3%B3gico+de+Tavira%2C+Tavira%2C+Portugal&amp;rft.aulast=Silva&amp;rft.aufirst=Lu%C3%ADs+Fraga+de&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.arqueotavira.com%2FMapas%2FIberia%2FPopuli.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AIberian+Peninsula">
